According to the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.fcc.gov/communications-business-opportunities/cybersecurity-small-businesses\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;U.S. Federal Communications Commission&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, theft of digital information has surpassed physical theft as the most commonly reported fraud for small businesses. &quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;what-even-is-an-agents-sdk\&quot;&gt;What even &lt;i&gt;is&lt;/i&gt; an Agents SDK?&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-even-is-an-agents-sdk\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;The AI landscape is evolving at an incredible pace, and with it, the tools and platforms available to developers are becoming more powerful and interconnected than ever. Here at Cloudflare, we&amp;#39;re genuinely passionate about empowering you to build the next generation of applications, and that absolutely includes intelligent agents that can reason, act, and interact with the world.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;When we talk about &amp;quot;&lt;b&gt;Agents SDKs&lt;/b&gt;&amp;quot;, it can sometimes feel a bitâ¦ fuzzy. Some SDKs (software development kits) &lt;b&gt;described as &amp;#39;agent&amp;#39; SDKs&lt;/b&gt; are really about providing frameworks for tool calling and interacting with models. They&amp;#39;re fantastic for defining an agent&amp;#39;s &amp;quot;brain&amp;quot; â its intelligence, its ability to reason, and how it uses external tools. Hereâs the thing: all these agents need a place to actually run. Then there&amp;#39;s what we offer at Cloudflare: &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/agents/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;an SDK purpose-built to provide a seamless execution layer for agents&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. While orchestration frameworks define how agents think, our SDK focuses on where they run, abstracting away infrastructure to enable persistent, scalable execution across our global network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Think of it as the ultimate shell, the place where any agent, defined by any agent SDK (like the powerful new OpenAI Agents SDK), can truly live, persist, and run at global scale.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Weâve chosen OpenAIâs Agents SDK for this example, but the infrastructure is not specific to it. The execution layer is designed to integrate with any agent runtime.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Thatâs what this post is about: what we built, what we learned, and the design patterns that emerged from fusing these two pieces together.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;why-use-two-sdks\&quot;&gt;Why use two SDKs?&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#why-use-two-sdks\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://openai.github.io/openai-agents-js/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;OpenAIâs Agents SDK&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; gives you the &lt;i&gt;agent&lt;/i&gt;: a reasoning loop, tool definitions, and memory abstraction. But it assumes you bring your own runtime and state.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/agents/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflareâs Agents SDK&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; gives you the &lt;i&gt;environment&lt;/i&gt;: a persistent object on our network with identity, state, and built-in concurrency control. But it doesnât tell you how your agent should behave.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;By combining them, we get a clear split:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;OpenAI&lt;/b&gt;: cognition, planning, tool orchestration&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Cloudflare&lt;/b&gt;: location, identity, memory, execution&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;This separation of concerns let us stay focused on logic, not glue code.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;what-you-can-build-with-persistent-agents\&quot;&gt;What you can build with persistent agents&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-you-can-build-with-persistent-agents\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;Cloudflare &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/durable-objects/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Durable Objects&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; let agents go beyond simple, stateless functions. They can persist memory, coordinate across workflows, and respond in real time. Combined with the OpenAI Agents SDK, this enables systems that reason, remember, and adapt over time.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Here are three architectural patterns that show how agents can be composed, guided, and connected:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Multi-agent systems: &lt;/b&gt;Divide responsibilities across specialized agents that collaborate on tasks.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Human-in-the-loop: &lt;/b&gt;Let agents plan independently but wait for human input at key decision points.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Addressable agents: &lt;/b&gt;Make agents reachable through real-world interfaces like phone calls or WebSockets.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;multi-agent-systems\&quot;&gt;Multi-agent systemsÂ &lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#multi-agent-systems\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Multi-agent systems let you break down a task into specialized agents that handle distinct responsibilities. In the example below, a triage agent routes questions to either a history or math tutor based on the query. Each agent has its own memory, logic, and instructions. With Cloudflare &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/durable-objects/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Durable Objects&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, these agents persist across sessions and can coordinate responses, making it easy to build systems that feel modular but work together intelligently.&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-TypeScript\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-TypeScript\&quot;&gt;export class MyAgent extends Agent {\n  async onRequest() {\n    const historyTutorAgent = new Agent({\n      instructions:\n        &amp;quot;You provide assistance with historical queries. Explain important events and context clearly.&amp;quot;,\n      name: &amp;quot;History Tutor&amp;quot;,\n    });\n\n    const mathTutorAgent = new Agent({\n      instructions:\n        &amp;quot;You provide help with math problems. Explain your reasoning at each step and include examples&amp;quot;,\n      name: &amp;quot;Math Tutor&amp;quot;,\n    });\n\n    const triageAgent = new Agent({\n      handoffs: [historyTutorAgent, mathTutorAgent],\n      instructions:\n        &amp;quot;You determine which agent to use based on the user&amp;#039;s homework question&amp;quot;,\n      name: &amp;quot;Triage Agent&amp;quot;,\n    });\n\n    const result = await run(triageAgent, &amp;quot;What is the capital of France?&amp;quot;);\n    return Response.json(result.finalOutput);\n  }\n}&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            \n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;human-in-the-loop\&quot;&gt;Human-in-the-loop&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#human-in-the-loop\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;We implemented a&lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/agents/tree/main/openai-sdk/human-in-the-loop\&quot;&gt; &lt;u&gt;human-in-the-loop agent example&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; using these two SDKs together. The goal: run an OpenAI agent with a planning loop, allow human decisions to intercept the plan, and preserve state across invocations via Durable Objects.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The architecture looked like this:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;An OpenAI &lt;code&gt;Agent&lt;/code&gt; instance runs inside a Durable Object&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;User submits a prompt&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The agent plans multiple steps&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;After each step, it yields control and waits for a human to approve or intervene&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;State (including memory and intermediate steps) is persisted in &lt;code&gt;this.state&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;It looks like this:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-TypeScript\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-TypeScript\&quot;&gt;export class MyAgent extends Agent {\n  // ...\n  async onStart() {\n    if (this.state.serialisedRunState) {\n      const runState = await RunState.fromString(\n        this.agent,\n        this.state.serialisedRunState\n      );\n      this.result = await run(this.agent, runState);&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;This design lets us intercept the agentâs plan at every step and store it. The client could then:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Fetch the pending step via another route&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Review or modify it&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Send approval or rejection back to the agent to resume execution&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is only possible because the agent lives inside a Durable Object. It has persistent memory and identity, allowing multi-turn interaction even across sessions&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;addressable-agents-call-my-agent\&quot;&gt;Addressable agents: âCall my Agentâ&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#addressable-agents-call-my-agent\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;One of the most interesting takeaways from this pattern is that agents are not just HTTP endpoints. Yes, you can &lt;code&gt;fetch() &lt;/code&gt;them via Durable Objects, but conceptually, &lt;b&gt;agents are addressable entities&lt;/b&gt; â and there&amp;#39;s no reason those addresses have to be tied to URLs.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;You could imagine agents reachable by phone call, by email, or via pub/sub systems. Durable Objects give each agent a global identity that can be referenced however you want.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In this design:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;External sources of input connect to the Cloudflare network; via email, HTTP, or any network interface. In this demo, we use Twilio to route a phone call to a WebSocket input on the Agent.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;The call is routed through Cloudflareâs infrastructure, so latency is low and identity is preserved.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;We also store the real-time state updates within the agent, so we can view it on a website (served by the agent itself). This is great for use cases like customer service and education.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-TypeScript\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-TypeScript\&quot;&gt;export class MyAgent extends Agent {\n  // receive phone calls via websocket\n  async onConnect(connection: Connection, ctx: ConnectionContext) {\n    if (ctx.request.url.includes(&amp;quot;media-stream&amp;quot;)) {\n      const agent = new RealtimeAgent({\n        instructions:\n          &amp;quot;You are a helpful assistant that starts every conversation with a creative greeting.&amp;quot;,\n        name: &amp;quot;Triage Agent&amp;quot;,\n      });\n\n      connection.send(`Welcome! You are connected with ID: ${connection.id}`);\n\n      const twilioTransportLayer = new TwilioRealtimeTransportLayer({\n        twilioWebSocket: connection,\n      });\n\n      const session = new RealtimeSession(agent, {\n        transport: twilioTransportLayer,\n      });\n\n      await session.connect({\n        apiKey: process.env.OPENAI_API_KEY as string,\n      });\n\n      session.on(&amp;quot;history_updated&amp;quot;, (history) =&amp;gt; {\n        this.setState({ history });\n      });\n    }\n  }\n}&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;This lets an agent become truly multimodal, accepting and outputting data as audio, video, text, email. This pattern opened up exciting possibilities for modular agents and long-running workflows where each agent focuses on a specific domain.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;what-we-learned-and-what-you-should-know\&quot;&gt;What we learned (and what you should know)&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#what-we-learned-and-what-you-should-know\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          \n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;1-openai-assumes-you-bring-your-own-state-cloudflare-gives-you-one\&quot;&gt;1. OpenAI assumes you bring your own state â Cloudflare gives you one&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#1-openai-assumes-you-bring-your-own-state-cloudflare-gives-you-one\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;OpenAIâs SDK is stateless by default. You can attach memory abstractions, but the SDK doesnât tell you where or how to persist it. Cloudflareâs Durable Objects, by contrast, &lt;i&gt;are&lt;/i&gt; persistent â thatâs the whole point. Every instance has a unique identity and storage API &lt;code&gt;(this.ctx.storage)&lt;/code&gt;. This means we can:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Store long-term memory across invocations&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Hydrate the agentâs memory before &lt;code&gt;run()&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Save any updates after &lt;code&gt;run()&lt;/code&gt; completes&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;2-durable-object-routing-isnt-just-routing-its-your-agent-factory\&quot;&gt;2. Durable Object routing isnât just routing â itâs your agent factory&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#2-durable-object-routing-isnt-just-routing-its-your-agent-factory\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;At first glance, &lt;code&gt;routeAgentRequest&lt;/code&gt; looks like a simple dispatcher: map a request to a Durable Object based on a URL. But it plays a deeper role â it defines the identity boundary for your agents. We realized this while trying to scope agent instances per user and per task.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;In Durable Objects, identity is tied to an ID. When you call &lt;code&gt;idFromName()&lt;/code&gt;, you get a stable, name-based ID that always maps to the same object. This means repeated calls with the same name return the same agent instance â along with its memory and state. In contrast, calling &lt;code&gt;.newUniqueId()&lt;/code&gt; creates a new, isolated object each time.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This is where routing becomes critical: it&amp;#39;s where you decide how long an agent should live, and what it should remember.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This lets us:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Spin up multiple agents per user (e.g. one per session or task)&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Co-locate memory and logic&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Avoid unintended memory sharing between conversations&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Gotcha:&lt;/b&gt; If you forget to use &lt;code&gt;idFromName()&lt;/code&gt; and just call &lt;code&gt;.newUniqueId()&lt;/code&gt;, youâll get a new agent each time, and your memory will never persist. This is a common early bug that silently kills statefulness.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h3 id=\&quot;3-agents-are-composable-and-thats-powerful\&quot;&gt;ââ3. Agents are composable â and thatâs powerful&lt;/h3&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#3-agents-are-composable-and-thats-powerful\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n        &lt;p&gt;Agents can invoke each other using Durable Object routing, forming workflows where each agent owns its own memory and logic. This enables composition â building systems from specialized parts that cooperate.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This makes agent architecture more like microservices â composable, stateful, and distributed.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;final-thoughts-building-agents-that-think-and-live\&quot;&gt;Final thoughts: building agents that think &lt;i&gt;and&lt;/i&gt; live&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#final-thoughts-building-agents-that-think-and-live\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;This pattern â OpenAI cognition + Cloudflare execution â worked better than we expected. It let us:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Write agents with full planning and memory&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Pause and resume them asynchronously&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Avoid building orchestration from scratch&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Compose multiple agents into larger systems&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;The hardest parts:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Correctly scoping agent architecture&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Persisting only valid state&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Debugging with good observability&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;At Cloudflare, we are incredibly excited to see what &lt;i&gt;you&lt;/i&gt; build with this powerful combination. public beta. Deploy simple, global, and programmable containers alongside your Workers. &quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;Weâre excited to announce that &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-containers-coming-2025/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Containers&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; are now available in beta for all users on paid plans.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can now run new kinds of applications alongside your Workers. From media and data processing at the edge, to backend services in any language, to CLI tools in batch workloads â Containers open up a world of possibilities.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Containers are tightly integrated with Workers and the rest of the developer platform, which means that:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Your workflow stays &lt;b&gt;simple&lt;/b&gt;: just define a Container in a few lines of code, and run&lt;code&gt; wrangler deploy&lt;/code&gt;, just like you would with a Worker.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Containers are &lt;b&gt;global: &lt;/b&gt;as with Workers, you just deploy to Region:Earth. No need to manage configs across 5 different regions for a global app.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can &lt;b&gt;use the right tool for the job&lt;/b&gt;: routing requests between Workers and Containers is easy. Use a Worker when you need to be ultra light-weight and scalable. Use a Container when you need more power and flexibility.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Containers are &lt;b&gt;programmable&lt;/b&gt;: container instances are spun up on-demand and controlled by Workers code. If you need custom logic, just write some JavaScript instead of spending time chaining together API calls or writing Kubernetes operators.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Want to try it today? Deploy your first Container-enabled Worker:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://deploy.workers.cloudflare.com/?url=https://github.com/cloudflare/templates/tree/main/containers-template\&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=\&quot;https://deploy.workers.cloudflare.com/button\&quot; alt=\&quot;Deploy to Cloudflare\&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;a-tour-of-containers\&quot;&gt;A tour of Containers&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#a-tour-of-containers\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;Letâs take a deeper look at Containers, using an example use case: code sandboxing.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letâs imagine that you want to run user-generated (or AI-generated) code as part of a platform youâre building. To do this, you want to spin up containers on demand. Each user needs their own isolated container, the users are distributed globally, and you need to start each container quickly so the users arenât waiting.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;You can set this up easily on Cloudflare Containers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Configuring a Container&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;p&gt;In your Worker, use the &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/cloudflare/containers\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Container class&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com//workers/wrangler/configuration/#containers\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;wrangler.jsonc&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to declare some basic configuration, such as your Containerâs default port, a sleep timeout, and which image to use, then route to it via the Worker.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;For each unique ID passed to the Containerâs binding, Cloudflare will spin up a new Container instance and route requests to it. When a new instance is requested, Cloudflare picks the best location across our global network where weâve pre-provisioned a ready-to-go container. This means that you can deploy a container close to an end user no matter where they are. And the initial container start takes just a few seconds. You donât have to worry about routing, provisioning, or scaling.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This example Worker will route requests to a unique container instance for each sandbox ID given at the path &lt;code&gt;/sandbox/ID&lt;/code&gt; and will be handled by standard Worker JavaScript otherwise:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-JavaScript\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-JavaScript\&quot;&gt;export class MyContainer extends Container {\n  defaultPort = 8080; // The default port for the container to listen on\n  sleepAfter = &amp;#039;5m&amp;#039;; // Sleep the container if no requests are made in this timeframe\n}\n\nexport default {\n  async fetch(request, env) {\n    const pathname = new URL(request.url).pathname;\n\n    // handle request with an on-demand container instance\n    if (pathname.startsWith(&amp;#039;/sandbox/&amp;#039;)) {\n      const sessionId = pathname.split(&amp;quot;/&amp;quot;)[2]\n      const containerInstance = getContainer(env.CONTAINER_SANDBOX, sessionId)\n      return await containerInstance.fetch(request);\n    }\n\n    // handle request with my Worker code otherwise\n    return myWorkerRequestHandler(request);\n  },\n};&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;h4&gt;Familiar and easy development workflow with &lt;code&gt;wrangler dev&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;p&gt;To configure which container image to use, you can provide an image URL in wrangler config or a path to a local Dockerfile.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;This config tells wrangler to use a locally defined image:&lt;/p&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-JSON\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-JSON\&quot;&gt;&amp;quot;containers&amp;quot;: [\n  {\n    &amp;quot;class_name&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;ContainerSandbox&amp;quot;,\n    &amp;quot;image&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;./Dockerfile&amp;quot;,\n    &amp;quot;max_instances&amp;quot;: 80,\n    &amp;quot;instance_type&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;basic&amp;quot;\n  }\n]&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;p&gt;When developing your application, you just run &lt;code&gt;wrangler dev&lt;/code&gt; and the container image will be automatically built and routable via your local Worker. This makes it easy to iterate on container code while making changes to your Worker at the same time. When you want to rebuild your image, just press âRâ on your keyboard from your terminal running &lt;code&gt;wrangler dev&lt;/code&gt;, and the Container is rebuilt and restarted.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Shipping your Container-enabled Worker to production with &lt;code&gt;wrangler deploy&lt;/code&gt;&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;p&gt;When itâs time to deploy, just run &lt;code&gt;wrangler deploy&lt;/code&gt;. Wrangler will push your image to your account, then it will be provisioned in various locations across Cloudflareâs global network.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;You donât have to worry about âartifact managementâ, or distribution, or auth, or jump through hoops to integrate your container with Workers. You just write your code and deploy it.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Observability is built-in&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;p&gt;Once your Container is in production, you have the visibility you need into how things are going, with end-to-end &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/developer-platform/products/workers-observability/\&quot;&gt;observability&lt;/a&gt;.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;From the Cloudflare dashboard, you can easily track status and resource usage across Container instances with built-in metrics:&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/1cMDL8qejpD9TnaVYgKeLD/cf42573c1315f0364c0d225bb77a76af/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1146\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;\nAnd if you need to dive deeper, you can dig into logs, which will be retained in the Cloudflare UI for seven days or &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/logs/about/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;pushed to an external sink&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; of your choice:&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2AusbmokynDaErssVFyu4A/3bb617ff9c2e488cdaee20612cb6bd15/image3.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1999\&quot; height=\&quot;1142\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Try it yourself&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;p&gt;Want to give it a shot? Check out &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/craigsdennis/sandboxing-day-containers\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;this example Worker for running sandboxed code&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; in a Container, and deploy it with one click.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Or better yet, if you have an image sitting around that youâve been dying to deploy to Cloudflare, you can get started with &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com//containers/get-started/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;our docs here&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.Â &lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;a-world-of-possibilities\&quot;&gt;A world of possibilities&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#a-world-of-possibilities\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;Weâre excited about all the new types of applications that are now possible to build on Workers. Weâve heard many of you tell us over the years that you would love to run your entire application on Cloudflare, if only you could deploy this one piece that needs to run in a container.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, you can run libraries that you couldn&amp;#39;t run in Workers before. For instance, try &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/megaconfidence/wifski/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;this Worker that uses FFmpeg to convert video to a GIF&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.Â &lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Or you can &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/mikenomitch/cron-container\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;run a container as part of a cron job&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Or deploy a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/mikenomitch/static-frontend-container-backend\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;static frontend with a containerized backend&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Or even run a &lt;a href=\&quot;https://github.com/ghostwriternr/claude-code-containers\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Cloudflare Agent that uses a Container to run Claude Code&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; on your behalf.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-containers-coming-2025/#integrating-with-more-of-cloudflares-developer-platform\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;integration with the rest of the Developer Platform&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; makes Containers even more powerful: &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-containers-coming-2025/#durable-objects-as-programmable-sidecars\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;use Durable Objects&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for state management, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/workflows/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Workflows&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/queues/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Queues&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://agents.cloudflare.com/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Agents&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to compose complex behaviors, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/r2/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;R2&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; to store Container data or media, and more.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;pricing-and-packaging\&quot;&gt;Pricing and packaging&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#pricing-and-packaging\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;As with the rest of our Cloudflare developer products, we wanted to apply the same principles to our developer platform with transparent pricing that scales up and down with your usage.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Today, you can select from the following instances at launch (and yes, we plan to add larger instances over time):  &lt;/p&gt;&lt;table&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Name&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Memory &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;CPU&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Disk&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;dev&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;256 MiB&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;1/16 vCPU&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;2 GB&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;basic&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;1 GiB&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;1/4 vCPU&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;4 GB&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;standard&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;4 GiB&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;1/2 vCPU&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td&gt;&lt;p&gt;4 GB&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;p&gt;You only pay for what you use âÂ charges start when a request is sent to the container or when it is manually started. Charges stop after the container instance goes to sleep, which can happen automatically after a timeout. This makes it easy to scale to zero, and allows you to get high utilization even with bursty traffic.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Containers are billed for every 10ms that they are actively running at the following rates, with monthly amounts included in &lt;i&gt;Workers Standard&lt;/i&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Memory&lt;/b&gt;: $0.0000025 per GiB-second, with 25 GiB-hours included&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;CPU&lt;/b&gt;: $0.000020 per vCPU-second, with 375 vCPU-minutes included&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Disk&lt;/b&gt; $0.00000007 per GB-second, with 200 GB-hours included&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Egress from Containers is priced at the following rates, with monthly amounts included in &lt;i&gt;Workers Standard&lt;/i&gt;:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;North America and Europe: $0.025 per GB with 1 TB included&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Australia, New Zealand, Taiwan, and Korea: $0.050 per GB with 500 GB included&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;Everywhere else: $0.040 per GB with 500 GB included&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;\nSee &lt;a href=\&quot;https://blog.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-containers-coming-2025/#pay-for-what-you-use-and-use-the-right-tool\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;our previous blog post&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; for a more in-depth look into pricing with an example app.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;whats-coming-next\&quot;&gt;Whatâs coming next?&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#whats-coming-next\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;With todayâs release, weâve only just begun to scratch the surface of what Containers will do on Workers. This is the first step of many towards our vision of a simple, global, and highly programmable Container platform.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Weâre already thinking about whatâs next, and wanted to give you a preview:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Higher limits and larger instances&lt;/b&gt; â We currently limit your concurrent instances to 40 total GiB of memory and 40 total vCPU. This is enough for some workloads, but many users will want to go higher âÂ  a lot higher. Select customers are already scaling well into the thousands of concurrent containers, and we want to bring this ability to more users. We will be raising our limits over the coming months to allow for more total containers and larger instance sizes.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Global autoscaling and latency-aware routing&lt;/b&gt; â Currently, containers are addressed by ID and started on-demand. For many use cases, users want to route to one of many stateless container instances deployed across the globe, then autoscale live instances automatically. Autoscaling will be activated with a single line of code, and will enable easy routing to the nearest ready instance.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;class MyBackend extends Container {\n  defaultPort = 8080;\n  autoscale = true; // global autoscaling on - new instances spin up when memory or CPU utilization is high\n}\n\n// routes requests to the nearest ready container and load balance globally\nasync fetch(request, env) {\n  return getContainer(env.MY_BACKEND).fetch(request);\n}&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;More ways to communicate between Containers and Workers&lt;/b&gt; â We will be adding more ways for your Worker to communicate with your container and vice versa. We will add an &lt;code&gt;exec&lt;/code&gt; command to run shell commands in your instance and handlers for HTTP requests &lt;i&gt;from&lt;/i&gt; the container to Workers. This will allow you to more easily extend your containers with functionality from the entire developer platform, reach out to other containers, and programmatically set up each container instance.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;\n            &lt;pre class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;&lt;code class=\&quot;language-Rust\&quot;&gt;class MyContainer extends Container {\n  // sets up container-to-worker communication with handlers\n  handlers = {\n    &amp;quot;example.cf&amp;quot;: &amp;quot;handleRequestFromContainer&amp;quot;\n  };\n\n  handleRequestFromContainer(req) {\n    return new Response(&amp;quot;You are responding from Workers to a Container request to a specific hostname&amp;quot;)\n  }\n\n  // use exec to run commands in your container instance\n  async cloneRepo(repoUrl) {\n    let command = this.exec(`git clone ${repoUrl}`)\n    await command.print()\n  }  \n}&lt;/pre&gt;&lt;/code&gt;\n            &lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;b&gt;Further integrations with the Developer Platform&lt;/b&gt; â We will continue to integrate with the developer platform with first-party APIs for our various services. We want it to be dead simple to mount &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/r2/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;R2 buckets&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, reach &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/hyperdrive/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Hyperdrive&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, access &lt;a href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/kv/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;KV&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, and more.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;And we are just getting started. Stay tuned for more updates this summer and over the course of the entire year.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;try-containers-today\&quot;&gt;Try Containers today&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#try-containers-today\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;The first step is to deploy your own container. Run &lt;code&gt;npm create cloudflare@latest -- --template=cloudflare/templates/containers-template&lt;/code&gt; or click the button below to deploy your first Container to Workers.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://deploy.workers.cloudflare.com/?url=https://github.com/cloudflare/templates/tree/main/containers-template\&quot;&gt;&lt;img src=\&quot;https://deploy.workers.cloudflare.com/button\&quot; alt=\&quot;Deploy to Cloudflare\&quot;/&gt;&lt;/a&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;\nWeâre excited to see all the ways you will use Containers. Deploy simple, global, and programmable containers alongside your Workers.&quot;],&quot;imgPreview&quot;:[0,&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/2qohvE4jKQaWEYiZ8rbbVH/3f9fb8a18b61a6a46961d1ea4cec3281/OG_Share_2024__60_.png&quot;]}],&quot;publicly_index&quot;:[0,true]}],[0,{&quot;id&quot;:[0,&quot;4Py1QO6TikGfaBeGSPBmFv&quot;],&quot;title&quot;:[0,&quot;Everything you need to know about NISTâs new guidance in âSP 1800-35: Implementing a Zero Trust Architectureâ&quot;],&quot;slug&quot;:[0,&quot;nist-sp-1300-85&quot;],&quot;excerpt&quot;:[0,&quot;We read NISTâs new guidance on âImplementing a Zero-Trust Architectureâ so that you donât have to.  Read this to get the key points on the newly-released NIST Special Publication 1800-35. &quot;],&quot;featured&quot;:[0,false],&quot;html&quot;:[0,&quot;&lt;p&gt;For decades, the United States &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.nist.gov/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;National Institute of Standards and Technology (NIST)&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; has been guiding industry efforts through the many publications in its &lt;a href=\&quot;https://csrc.nist.gov/\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;Computer Security Resource Center&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. NIST has played an especially important role in the adoption of Zero Trust architecture, through its series of publications that began with &lt;a href=\&quot;https://csrc.nist.gov/pubs/sp/800/207/final\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;NIST SP 800-207: Zero Trust Architecture&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, released in 2020.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;NIST has released another Special Publication in this series, &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.1800-35.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 1800-35&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, titled &amp;quot;Implementing a Zero Trust Architecture (ZTA)&amp;quot; which aims to provide practical steps and &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/access-management/how-to-implement-zero-trust/\&quot;&gt;best practices for deploying ZTA&lt;/a&gt; across various environments.Â  NISTâs publications about ZTA have been extremely influential across the industry, but are often lengthy and highly detailed, so this blog provides a short and easier-to-read summary of NISTâs latest guidance on ZTA.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;And so, in this blog post:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;We summarize the key items you need to know about this new NIST publication, which presents a reference architecture for &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/learning/security/glossary/what-is-zero-trust/\&quot;&gt;Zero Trust Architecture (ZTA)&lt;/a&gt; along with a series of âBuildsâ that demonstrate how different products from various vendors can be combined to construct a ZTA that complies with the reference architecture.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;We show how &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.cloudflare.com/zero-trust/products/\&quot;&gt;Cloudflareâs Zero Trust product suite&lt;/a&gt; can be integrated with offerings from other vendors to support a Zero Trust Architecture that maps to the NISTâs reference architecture.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;p&gt;We highlight a few key features of Cloudflareâs Zero Trust platform that are especially valuable to customers seeking compliance with NISTâs ZTA reference architecture, including compliance with FedRAMP and new post-quantum cryptography standards.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;p&gt;Letâs dive into NISTâs special publication!&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;overview-of-sp-1800-35\&quot;&gt;Overview of SP 1800-35&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#overview-of-sp-1800-35\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot; d=\&quot;m12.11 15.39-3.88 3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1-3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0-3.5l3.88-3.88a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-3.88 3.89a4.48 4.48 0 0 0 6.33 6.33l3.89-3.88a1 1 0 1 0-1.42-1.42Zm8.58-12.08a4.49 4.49 0 0 0-6.33 0l-3.89 3.88a1 1 0 0 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.88a2.52 2.52 0 0 1 3.5 0 2.47 2.47 0 0 1 0 3.5l-3.88 3.88a1 1 0 1 0 1.42 1.42l3.88-3.89a4.49 4.49 0 0 0 0-6.33ZM8.83 15.17a1 1 0 0 0 1.1.22 1 1 0 0 0 .32-.22l4.92-4.92a1 1 0 0 0-1.42-1.42l-4.92 4.92a1 1 0 0 0 0 1.42Z\&quot;&gt;&lt;/path&gt;&lt;/svg&gt;\n            &lt;/a&gt;\n          &lt;/div&gt;\n          &lt;p&gt;In &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.1800-35.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 1800-35&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, NIST reminds us that:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;A zero-trust architecture (ZTA) enables secure authorized access to assets â machines, applications and services running on them, and associated data and resources â whether located on-premises or in the cloud, for a hybrid workforce and partners based on an organizationâs defined access policy.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;NIST uses the term Subject to refer to entities (i.e. employees, developers, devices) that require access to Resources (i.e. computers, databases, servers, applications).Â  &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.1800-35.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 1800-35&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; focuses on developing and demonstrating various ZTA implementations that allow Subjects to access Resources. Specifically, the reference architecture in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.1800-35.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 1800-35&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; focuses mainly on &lt;i&gt;EIG&lt;/i&gt; or âEnhanced Identity Governanceâ, a specific approach to Zero Trust Architecture, which is defined by NIST in &lt;a href=\&quot;https://doi.org/10.6028/NIST.SP.800-207\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 800-207&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;For [the EIG] approach, enterprise resource access policies are based on identity and assigned attributes.Â &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;The primary requirement for [R]esource access is based on the access privileges granted to the given [S]ubject. Other factors such as device used, asset status, and environmental factors may alter the final confidence level calculation â¦ or tailor the result in some way, such as granting only partial access to a given [Resource] based on network location.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;Individual [R]esources or [policy enforcement points (PEP)] must have a way to forward requests to a policy engine service or authenticate the [S]ubject and approve the request before granting access.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/blockquote&gt;&lt;p&gt;While there are other approaches to ZTA mentioned in the original NIST &lt;a href=\&quot;https://doi.org/10.6028/NIST.SP.800-207\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 800-207&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, we omit those here because &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.1800-35.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 1800-35&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; focuses mostly on EIG.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The ZTA reference architecture from &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.1800-35.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 1800-35&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; focuses on EIG approaches as a set of logical components as shown in the figure below.Â  Each component in the reference architecture does not necessarily correspond directly to physical (hardware or software) components, or products sold by a single vendor, but rather to the logical functionality of the component.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;figure class=\&quot;kg-card kg-image-card\&quot;&gt;\n          &lt;Image src=\&quot;https://cf-assets.www.cloudflare.com/zkvhlag99gkb/hXSpBQINdjqyl57by3Uhc/fd39f66cebc2dd0a79dc4749b02208f3/image4.png\&quot; alt=\&quot;\&quot; class=\&quot;kg-image\&quot; width=\&quot;1314\&quot; height=\&quot;846\&quot; loading=\&quot;lazy\&quot;/&gt;\n          &lt;/figure&gt;&lt;p&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;Figure 1: General ZTA Reference Architecture. Source: NIST, &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.1800-35.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;u&gt;Special Publication 1800-35&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;sup&gt;&lt;i&gt;, &amp;quot;Implementing a Zero Trust Architecture (ZTA)â, 2025.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/sup&gt;&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The logical components in the reference architecture are all related to the implementation of policy. Policy is crucial for ZTA because the whole point of a ZTA is to apply policies that determine who has access to what, when and under what conditions.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The core components of the reference architecture are as follows:&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;| Policy Enforcement Point(PEP) | The PEP protects the âtrust zonesâ that host enterprise Resources, and handles enabling, monitoring, and eventually terminating connections between Subjects and Resources.  You can think of the PEP as the dataplane that supports the Subjectâs access to the Resources.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div style=\&quot;margin-left:0pt;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot; align=\&quot;left\&quot;&gt;\n    &lt;figure class=\&quot;table\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;table class=\&quot;ck-table-resized\&quot; width=\&quot;180\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;/colgroup&gt;\n            &lt;tbody&gt;\n                &lt;tr style=\&quot;height:21pt;\&quot;&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-align:center;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;Policy Enforcement Point&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;(PEP)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;The PEP protects the âtrust zonesâ that host enterprise Resources, and handles enabling, monitoring, and eventually terminating connections between Subjects and Resources.&amp;nbsp; You can think of the PEP as the dataplane that supports the Subjectâs access to the Resources.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                &lt;/tr&gt;\n                &lt;tr style=\&quot;height:21pt;\&quot;&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-align:center;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;Policy Engine&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-align:center;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;(PE)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;The PE handles the ultimate decision to grant, deny, or revoke access to a Resource for a given Subject, and calculates the trust scores/confidence levels and ultimate access decisions based on enterprise policy and information from supporting components.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                &lt;/tr&gt;\n                &lt;tr style=\&quot;height:21pt;\&quot;&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-align:center;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;Policy Administrator&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-align:center;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;(PA)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;The PA executes the PEâs policy decision by sending commands to the PEP to establish and terminate the communications path between the Subject and the Resource.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                &lt;/tr&gt;\n                &lt;tr style=\&quot;height:21pt;\&quot;&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-align:center;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;Policy Decision Point (PDP)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;The PDP is where the decision as to whether or not to permit a Subject to access a Resource is made.&amp;nbsp; The PIP included the Policy Engine (PE) and the Policy Administrator (PA).&amp;nbsp; You can think of the PDP as the control plane that controls the Subjectâs access to the Resources.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                &lt;/tr&gt;\n            &lt;/tbody&gt;\n        &lt;/table&gt;\n    &lt;/figure&gt;\n&lt;/div&gt;&lt;p&gt;The PDP operates on inputs from Policy Information Points (PIPs) which are supporting components that provide critical data and policy rules to the Policy Decision Point (PDP).&lt;/p&gt;&lt;div style=\&quot;margin-left:0pt;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot; align=\&quot;left\&quot;&gt;\n    &lt;figure class=\&quot;table\&quot;&gt;\n        &lt;table class=\&quot;ck-table-resized\&quot; style=\&quot;border-collapse:collapse;border-style:none;\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;colgroup&gt;\n                &lt;col style=\&quot;width:33.33%;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;Policy Information Point&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.2;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;text-align:center;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;(PIP)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                    &lt;/td&gt;\n                    &lt;td style=\&quot;border-color:#999999;border-width:1.5pt;overflow-wrap:break-word;overflow:hidden;padding:5pt;vertical-align:top;\&quot;&gt;\n                        &lt;p style=\&quot;line-height:1.38;margin-bottom:0pt;margin-top:0pt;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;The PIPs provide various types of telemetry and other information needed for the PDP to make informed access decisions.&amp;nbsp; Some PIPs include:&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/p&gt;\n                        &lt;ul style=\&quot;margin-bottom:0;margin-top:0;padding-inline-start:48px;\&quot;&gt;\n                            &lt;li style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;list-style-type:disc;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot; aria-level=\&quot;1\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;ICAM, or Identity, Credential, and Access Management, covering user authentication, single sign-on, user groups and access control features that are typically offered by Identity Providers (IdPs) like Okta, AzureAD or Ping Identity.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/li&gt;\n                            &lt;li style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;list-style-type:disc;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre;\&quot; dir=\&quot;ltr\&quot; aria-level=\&quot;1\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;Endpoint security includes endpoint detection and response (EDR) or endpoint protection platforms (EPP) that protect end user devices like laptops and mobile devices.&amp;nbsp; An EPP primarily focuses on preventing known threats using features like antivirus protection. Meanwhile, an EDR actively detects and responds to threats that may have already breached initial defenses using forensics, behavioral analysis and incident response tools. EDR and EPP products are offered by vendors like&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a style=\&quot;text-decoration:none;\&quot; target=\&quot;_blank\&quot; rel=\&quot;noopener noreferrer\&quot; href=\&quot;https://developers.cloudflare.com/cloudflare-one/identity/devices/service-providers/crowdstrike/\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#1155cc;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;-webkit-text-decoration-skip:none;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration-skip-ink:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;CrowdStrike&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;background-color:transparent;color:#000000;font-family:Arial,sans-serif;font-size:11pt;\&quot;&gt;&lt;span style=\&quot;font-style:normal;font-variant:normal;font-weight:400;text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline;white-space:pre-wrap;\&quot;&gt;,&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a style=\&quot;text-decoration:none;\&quot; introduces two more detailed reference architectures, the âCrawl Phaseâ and the âRun Phaseâ.Â  The âRun Phaseâ corresponds to the reference architecture that is shown in the figure above.Â  The âCrawl Phaseâ is a simplified version of this reference architecture that only deals with protecting on-premise Resources, and omits cloud Resources. Both of these phases focused on Enhanced Identity Governance approaches to ZTA, as we defined above. &lt;a href=\&quot;https://www.nccoe.nist.gov/sites/default/files/2024-11/zta-nist-sp-1800-35-ipd.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;NIST stated&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt;, &amp;quot;&lt;i&gt;We are skipping the EIG walk phase and have proceeded directly to the run phase&lt;/i&gt;&amp;quot;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;The &lt;a href=\&quot;https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.1800-35.pdf\&quot;&gt;&lt;u&gt;SP 1800-35&lt;/u&gt;&lt;/a&gt; then provides a sequence of detailed instructions, called âBuildsâ, that show how to implement âCrawl Phaseâ and âRun Phaseâ reference architectures using products sold by various vendors.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;p&gt;Since Cloudflareâs Zero Trust platform natively supports access to both cloud and on-premise resources, we will skip over the âCrawl Phaseâ and move directly to showing how Cloudflareâs Zero Trust platform can be used to support âRun Phaseâ of the reference architecture.&lt;/p&gt;\n          &lt;div class=\&quot;flex anchor relative\&quot;&gt;\n            &lt;h2 id=\&quot;a-complete-zero-trust-architecture-using-cloudflare-and-integrations\&quot;&gt;A complete Zero Trust Architecture using Cloudflare and integrations&lt;/h2&gt;\n            &lt;a href=\&quot;#a-complete-zero-trust-architecture-using-cloudflare-and-integrations\&quot; aria-hidden=\&quot;true\&quot; class=\&quot;relative sm:absolute sm:-left-5\&quot;&gt;\n              &lt;svg width=\&quot;16\&quot; height=\&quot;16\&quot; viewBox=\&quot;0 0 24 24\&quot;&gt;&lt;path fill=\&quot;currentcolor\&quot;
